‚ĚĮ /compound-engineering:ce-brainstorm You are a senior product manager at an AI 
 data services company that creates high-quality training data for fine-tuning  
large language models (LLMs). Your task is to write a comprehensive Product     
Requirements Document (PRD) for "RLHF DataForge" ‚ÄĒ a unified task configuration 
 and data collection platform that enables human annotators to create training  
data for LLM alignment using Reinforcement Learning from Human Feedback (RLHF). 
This platform has two interfaces:                                               
                                                                                
1. Task Configuration Tool (Admin Interface): An admin-facing tool where ML     
engineers and data managers define the parameters for annotation tasks ‚ÄĒ        
analogous to a Google Form creation screen but purpose-built for RLHF.          
2. Data Collection Interface (Annotator Interface): The annotator-facing tool   
where human workers interact with AI models, compare responses, and provide     
preference feedback ‚ÄĒ this is the "form" that annotators fill out.              
The platform must be flexible enough to support the data collection             
methodologies used by both Anthropic and Meta in their landmark RLHF research,  
as well as hybrid and custom approaches.                                        
                                                                                
                                                                                
PRODUCT REQUIREMENTS                                                            
Using the research context above, write a comprehensive PRD                     
                                                                                
* Executive Summary                                                             
                                                                                
* Problem Statement                                                             
* User Personas                                                                 
   * Define at least three personas:                                            
      * Task Administrator / ML Engineer (configures tasks)                     
      * Human Annotator / Crowdworker (performs annotations)                    
      * Data Consumer / Training Engineer (consumes exported data for model     
training) Include their goals, pain points, and how they interact with the      
platform.                                                                       
* Product Scope & Core Modules                                                  
   * Module 1 ‚ÄĒ Task Configuration Engine (Admin Interface): template library   
for known configurations of data needs and configurable parameters for custom   
task types                                                                      
   * Module 2 ‚ÄĒ Data Collection Interface (Annotator Interface) This interface  
should support interface for different tasks type                               
   * Module 3 ‚ÄĒ Quality & Analytics Dashboard                                   
   * Module 4 ‚ÄĒ Data Export & Pipeline Integration                              
   * Any other module that should be included but I may have missed.            
* Detailed Feature Specifications                                               
* Information Architecture & Wireframe Descriptions.                            
                                                                                
Think from first principles and do not try to one shot this requirement         
document. I gave you the outline upfront so that we know what is in scope. Go   
through the research paper and start by listing  goals we want to achieve and   
list of usecases. Identify core data needs based on the research papers         
attached so that we can model the platform in a way that supports meeting       
generic data of any LLM provider out there. It is a brainstorming so ask me     
questions if needed.

  ---
  Research Synthesis

  Key Findings from Papers

  Anthropic (2204.05862v1) ‚ÄĒ "Training a Helpful and Harmless Assistant with
  RLHF":
  - Core format: pairwise comparison in multi-turn, real-time conversations with
   models
  - Two task modes: helpfulness (pick better response) and red-teaming (pick
  more harmful response)
  - Preference strength captured but only used to filter near-ties
  - Lightweight QC: writing-quality spot-checks, no IAA-based filtering. ~63%
  agreement was "sufficient"
  - Weekly model hot-swapping during online data collection phase
  - Annotators could edit model responses (late addition, <10% of data)
  - 3 data tranches: base (86k), rejection sampling (54k), online (22k)

  Meta/Llama 2 (2307.09288v2) ‚ÄĒ "Llama 2: Open Foundation and Fine-Tuned Chat
  Models":
  - Also pairwise comparison, but with a 4-point preference degree scale
  (significantly better ‚Üí negligibly better)
  - Preference margin fed directly into reward model loss ‚ÄĒ richer signal
  - Two separate reward models (helpfulness RM + safety RM)
  - Rigorous 4-step annotator qualification process + manual QA review by
  content managers
  - Annotators write their own prompts (not selected from a pool)
  - 14 weekly batches, 1.4M+ comparisons total
  - Safety annotations include a 3-bin safety label + risk category taxonomy
  - Curriculum strategy: simple prompts early, complex later
  - Key insight: "Quality is all you need" ‚ÄĒ 27k high-quality SFT annotations
  beat millions of low-quality ones

  Critical Differences to Support

  Competitive Landscape

  Gap in the market: No single tool combines a polished RLHF-specific annotation
   UI + workforce management + configurable QC + training-framework integration.
   Argilla is closest (open-source) but lacks workforce management and advanced
  QC. Commercial platforms (Scale AI, Surge AI) are expensive, black-box, and
  create vendor lock-in.

  ---
  Proposed Goals & Use Cases

  Based on the research, here are the core goals and use cases I see for RLHF
  DataForge:

  Goals

  1. Methodology-agnostic: Support Anthropic-style (real-time multi-turn),
  Meta-style (batch pre-generated), and hybrid approaches from a single
  configurable platform
  2. Full RLHF data lifecycle: Prompt curation ‚Üí response generation ‚Üí
  annotation ‚Üí quality analysis ‚Üí export ‚Üí iteration
  3. Configurable annotation dimensions: Binary preference, n-point scales,
  multi-dimensional rubrics, safety labels, free-text justifications ‚ÄĒ all
  mix-and-matchable per task
  4. Production-grade quality pipeline: From lightweight crowd approaches to
  rigorous qualification-gated expert workflows
  5. Training-framework-native export: DPO, PPO, reward model formats out of the
   box (TRL/HuggingFace compatible)

  Core Use Cases (derived from papers)

  1. SFT data collection ‚ÄĒ Annotators write prompt-response pairs (Meta Stage 1)
  2. Pairwise preference annotation ‚ÄĒ Compare two model responses, pick
  preferred (both papers)
  3. Multi-turn conversational RLHF ‚ÄĒ Real-time multi-turn dialogue with
  comparison at each turn (Anthropic)
  4. Safety/red-teaming data collection ‚ÄĒ Adversarial prompts + safety
  classification (both papers)
  5. Response editing/rewriting ‚ÄĒ Annotators improve model outputs (Anthropic,
  late feature)
  6. Model evaluation (Elo/Arena) ‚ÄĒ Blind head-to-head model comparison
  (Anthropic Elo, LMSYS-style)
  7. Iterative campaign management ‚ÄĒ Multiple RLHF rounds with model improvement
   between batches (Meta V1-V5, Anthropic online)
  8. Annotator qualification & routing ‚ÄĒ Skill-based assignment with
  qualification tests (Meta 4-step)

  ---
  Now before I go further, I want to pressure-test the scope with you.

  ‚éŅ ¬†¬∑ The research reveals a wide spectrum of RLHF data collection patterns. 
     Before I model the platform, what is the primary deployment context for

     ¬∑ How should we handle the model integration layer? This affects whether

     infrastructure. ‚Üí BYOM only

‚Źļ Good ‚ÄĒ that sharpens the scope significantly:

  - SaaS multi-tenant ‚ÄĒ tenant isolation, self-service onboarding, billing
  - BYOM ‚ÄĒ admins configure external model API endpoints, platform orchestrates
  prompt/response flow
  - Managed internal workforce ‚ÄĒ qualification, assignment, performance
  tracking, payment all built in

  else sits on. Based on the two papers, I've identified these core annotation 
  task types that the platform must support:

    - Module 6: Platform Administration ‚ÄĒ multi-tenancy, billing, security, API

  - Configurable QC pipeline with 8 building blocks from lightweight to rigorous
  - Full campaign management with cross-round analytics (tracks the Meta finding

  - Response positional bias detection and randomization

‚Źļ Still running. I'll wait for the notification. In the meantime, here are the
  findings from the two completed reviews:

  ---
  Document Review Findings (2 of 3 complete)

  Coherence Review ‚ÄĒ 11 findings

  High confidence:
  1. Campaign scope ambiguity ‚ÄĒ campaign_id is nullable on annotations, meaning
  annotations can exist outside campaigns, contradicting the model where all
  RLHF data is campaign-bound
  2. Requirements scattered across sections ‚ÄĒ Real-time model interaction
  requirements appear in 4 different sections with no single authoritative
  location

  Moderate confidence (actionable):
  3. Data mixing vs. lineage traceability ‚ÄĒ Exporting mixed-round data with
  weights obscures which round each point came from, contradicting the "full
  traceability" promise
  4. Non-streaming API fallback UX undefined ‚ÄĒ timeout, UX degradation, and
  acceptability thresholds not specified
  5. Full manual review process lacks execution details ‚ÄĒ who reviews, SLA, what
   happens on rejection
  6. Gold standards vs. qualification tests operate independently with no clear
  interaction model
  7. "Recalibration" vs. "recertification" ‚ÄĒ two different terms, unclear if
  same or different process
  8. Margin-based loss metadata ‚ÄĒ annotator agreement as training signal
  referenced in persona goals but never defined
  9. Managed internal workforce positioning contradicts the implicit need for
  crowdsourcing at scale
  10. Response editing ‚ÄĒ unclear if it's a standalone task type or a feature
  within pairwise tasks
  11. Preference polarity applicability to different task types not specified

  Scope Review ‚ÄĒ 9 findings

  Scope exceeds goals (HIGH):
  1. Compensation management (Module 3.4) ‚ÄĒ payroll, bonus triggers, per-task
  rates serve crowd-labor ops, not the internal-workforce personas described
  2. Elo Model Arena ‚ÄĒ model evaluation, not data collection. No persona goal
  served.
  3. Demographics field in annotator profile has no consumer
  4. Five simultaneous IAA algorithms ‚ÄĒ framework-ahead-of-need; one
  configurable metric (Gwet's AC2 per research) suffices

  Scope exceeds goals (MODERATE):
  5. Qualification test builder is a full form-builder product nested inside an
  annotation platform
  6. Deduplication + train/test splitting in export layer duplicates training
  pipeline responsibility
  7. Python SDK adds no capability beyond REST API + OpenAPI spec

  Missing from data model (HIGH):
  8. No task_instance_id ‚ÄĒ needed to group overlapping annotator records for IAA
   computation
  9. No is_complete flag on responses ‚ÄĒ interrupted streaming responses could
  silently enter training data

  I'll share the feasibility review when it lands. Would you like me to start
  addressing any of these findings now, or wait for the complete picture?

‚Źļ Agent "Review PRD for feasibility" completed

‚Źļ All three reviews are complete. Here's the consolidated picture:

  ---
  Consolidated Review Summary

  Feasibility Review ‚ÄĒ 8 findings

  Architecture blockers (HIGH):
  1. No technology stack decisions ‚ÄĒ language, database, hosting, frontend
  framework all unspecified. Several requirements (real-time streaming proxy,
  multi-tenant isolation, async exports) implicitly constrain architecture
  without acknowledging it.
  2. Real-time model proxy underspecified ‚ÄĒ timeout asymmetry (Model A: 2s,
  Model B: 45s), API rate limiting across concurrent annotators, and credential
  rotation for customer API keys are all missing.
  3. Multi-tenancy isolation strategy unresolved ‚ÄĒ tenant_id missing from
  annotation record schema. Row-level vs. schema-per-tenant vs.
  database-per-tenant not decided ‚ÄĒ affects every query and migration.

  Implementation risks (MODERATE):
  4. Compensation module has regulatory implications ‚ÄĒ worker classification,
  tax reporting, payment processing vs. tracking-only not clarified
  5. Dataset snapshot reproducibility ‚ÄĒ requires either full-copy storage
  (expensive) or event-sourced architecture (complex). Neither specified.
  6. N-way ranking decomposition ‚ÄĒ ties + pairwise decomposition behavior
  undefined. N=8 produces 28 pairs per annotation, multiplying export volume.
  7. Deduplication ‚ÄĒ "configurable similarity threshold" hides an algorithm
  choice (hash, LSH, embedding) with major performance implications
  8. Elo concurrent updates ‚ÄĒ sequential by nature, but concurrent annotators
  need a consistency strategy

  Positive note: The reviewer praised the document as "exceptionally thorough as
   a product requirements document" with well-defined schemas, specific API
  contracts, and unambiguous wireframes.

  ---
  Action Items ‚ÄĒ What to Address

  Across all 3 reviews, the findings cluster into three categories:

  A. Data Model Fixes (should fix now)

  These are schema gaps that affect correctness:
  - Add tenant_id to annotation record schema
  - Add task_instance_id to group overlapping annotator records for IAA
  - Add is_complete flag on responses for interrupted streams
  - Clarify campaign_id nullability ‚ÄĒ can annotations exist outside campaigns?

  B. Scope Questions (need your input)

  - Compensation module ‚ÄĒ Keep, simplify to tracking-only, or defer?
  - Elo Model Arena ‚ÄĒ Keep as data collection task type, or descope?
  - 5 IAA algorithms ‚ÄĒ Ship all 5 or start with Gwet's AC2 only?
  - Deduplication in export ‚ÄĒ Keep or leave to training pipeline?
  - Demographics field ‚ÄĒ Keep or remove?

  C. Feasibility Notes (address in technical design, not PRD)

  The feasibility reviewer correctly identified that this is a PRD, not a
  technical design doc. Stack selection, isolation strategy, streaming
  architecture, and snapshot mechanisms are appropriately deferred to a
  planning/architecture phase.

‚Źļ All 12 screens captured. Here's my comprehensive review comparing the Paper
  designs against the PRD requirements:

  ---
  Design Review: Paper Screens vs. PRD Requirements

  Overall Verdict

  The screens are strongly aligned with the PRD direction. The design system is
  cohesive (teal accent, warm neutrals, Inter/Literata/JetBrains Mono type
  stack), and the information architecture matches the PRD's navigation
  structure. The designs look professional and functional ‚ÄĒ not "AI slop." That
  said, there are gaps and a few areas where the designs diverge from
  requirements.

  ---
  Screen-by-Screen Review

  Screen 01 ‚ÄĒ Admin Dashboard ‚ÄĒ Excellent match
  - KPI cards (Annotations, Active Annotators, IAA, Active Campaigns) match PRD
  Section 6.2 exactly
  - Campaign Progress with progress bars and annotation counts present
  - Quality Alerts panel with color-coded severity (yellow, pink, blue) ‚ÄĒ good
  addition over the PRD wireframe
  - Annotation Volume chart with 4 series (Helpfulness, Safety, SFT, Arena)
  matches PRD
  - Left nav structure matches PRD IA: Admin > Workforce > Quality > Data
  sections
  - Time period selector ("Last 7 days") and org switcher ("Alignment Lab")
  present

  Screen 02 ‚ÄĒ Task Template Picker ‚ÄĒ Excellent match
  - All 8 templates present: Pairwise Preference, Multi-Turn Chat, SFT Data
  Authoring, Safety/Red-Teaming, Response Editing, N-Way Ranking, Rubric
  Scoring, Model Arena
  - Source attribution on each card (Anthropic, Meta, LMSYS, etc.) matches PRD
  - "Start from Scratch" option at bottom matches PRD
  - Clean card grid layout with icons ‚ÄĒ good visual differentiation

  Screen 03 ‚ÄĒ Task Configuration Builder ‚ÄĒ Good match, minor note
  - Section stepper (Basic Info, Prompts, Models, Annotation, Quality,
  Guidelines, Review) matches the PRD's multi-step flow
  - Preference Scale options (4-point, Binary, 7-point, Custom) present
  - Preference Polarity dropdown, Allow Ties toggle, Additional Inputs
  checkboxes all match PRD
  - Constraints section (min time, allow skip/flag) present
  - Back / Next navigation present
  - Preview and Save Draft buttons in header ‚ÄĒ good
  - Note: PRD wireframe shows the current section is "Annotation" (step 4) with
  green checkmarks on completed steps ‚ÄĒ design matches this

  Screen 04 ‚ÄĒ Campaign Round Detail ‚ÄĒ Excellent match
  - Round header with status badge ("ACTIVE"), breadcrumb to campaign
  - Three KPI cards: Progress, IAA (Gwet's AC2), Preference Distribution ‚ÄĒ
  matches PRD Section 6.9
  - Model Versions section showing Model A and Model B with version labels
  - Cross-Round Comparison table with all 6 metrics from the PRD (IAA, Gold
  Accuracy, % Sig better, % Negligible, Avg time/task, Annotations)
  - The insight callout at bottom ("Significantly better declining...consistent
  with model convergence per Meta Llama 2 findings") is a great touch ‚ÄĒ directly
   from the PRD
  - "Advance to Review" and "Export Round Data" CTAs present

  Screen 05 ‚ÄĒ Pairwise Preference Annotation ‚ÄĒ Excellent match
  - Full-width annotator interface (no admin sidebar ‚ÄĒ correct, annotator has
  separate entry point)
  - Header bar with task name, progress (47/200), timer, Guidelines, Flag, Skip
  - Prompt displayed prominently
  - Side-by-side Response A / Response B panels with token counts
  - Code block rendering with syntax highlighting ‚ÄĒ addresses PRD's markdown
  rendering requirement
  - 7-point preference scale implemented as a horizontal button row ("Sig.
  better ‚ÄĒ A is better ‚ÄĒ Slightly ‚ÄĒ Tie ‚ÄĒ Slightly ‚ÄĒ B is better ‚ÄĒ Sig. better")
   ‚ÄĒ this is a nice interpretation, though the task config shows "4-point" was
  selected. May want to verify consistency.
  - Justification field (required) at bottom with Submit button showing keyboard
   shortcut (Enter)

  Screen 06 ‚ÄĒ Multi-Turn Conversational RLHF ‚ÄĒ Excellent match
  - Conversation history at top with clear You/Assistant turn markers
  - Turn choice badges ("A chosen at Turn 1", "B chosen at Turn 2") ‚ÄĒ great UX,
  matches PRD
  - Dual response panels below with streaming indicators ("Streaming..." vs
  "Complete")
  - Streaming progress bar on Response A ‚ÄĒ nice detail
  - Binary preference buttons ("A is better" / "B is better") at bottom
  - Message input with "Send Shift+Enter" ‚ÄĒ matches PRD
  - Turn counter (Turn 3/6) in header

  Screen 07 ‚ÄĒ Safety Red-Teaming ‚ÄĒ Excellent match
  - Content warning banner at top with "Report Disturbing Content" button and
  break timer ("Break in: 18 min") ‚ÄĒ all from PRD
  - Adversarial prompt labeled clearly
  - Side-by-side responses with a red warning callout on Response A ("Contains
  specific technical details about bypassing security") ‚ÄĒ nice safety signal not
   in the PRD but a good addition
  - Bottom bar: preference ("Which is safer?"), Safety Classification (3-bin
  radio), Risk Category dropdown, Attack Vector dropdown ‚ÄĒ all match PRD Section
   6.7
  - Submit button present

  Screen 08 ‚ÄĒ Annotator Home / Task Queue ‚ÄĒ Good match, one gap
  - Separate header ("DATAFORGE ANNOTATOR" badge) ‚ÄĒ correctly differentiates
  from admin interface
  - KPI cards: Today (47), This Week (186), Quality (Gold 82%, Peer IAA 0.76) ‚ÄĒ
  match PRD
  - Task queue with 3 tasks, each showing type badge (Pairwise, Safety, Arena),
  remaining count, time estimate
  - Safety task has warning icon and "Adversarial testing" label ‚ÄĒ good
  - Qualification Tests section at bottom ‚ÄĒ matches PRD
  - Recent Activity feed ‚ÄĒ matches PRD
  - Gap: PRD wireframe (Section 6.12) shows progress bars under the daily/weekly
   targets. The design shows flat numbers without progress bars ‚ÄĒ minor but
  useful visual.
  - Gap: Large empty space between the task queue (3 items) and the bottom
  sections. The layout could be tighter.

  Screen 09 ‚ÄĒ N-Way Ranking ‚ÄĒ Excellent match
  - Prompt at top, "Drag to rank" instruction
  - 4 responses displayed vertically with rank numbers (1-4) and up/down
  chevrons for reordering
  - Token counts on each response ‚ÄĒ matches PRD
  - Rank 1 item has a subtle teal highlight ‚ÄĒ good visual affordance showing
  "top ranked"
  - Submit Ranking button with Enter shortcut
  - Note: PRD mentions "Expand" toggles per response ‚ÄĒ design shows truncated
  responses but no explicit expand control. For longer responses this would be
  needed.

  Screen 10 ‚ÄĒ Quality Dashboard ‚ÄĒ Good match, some elements condensed
  - IAA trend chart (Gwet's AC2) with Helpfulness, Safety, Overall lines ‚ÄĒ
  matches PRD
  - Target (0.80) and Threshold (0.65) reference lines ‚ÄĒ matches PRD Section
  6.10
  - Annotator Performance table with Gold Acc, Peer IAA, Tasks/hr, Status
  columns ‚ÄĒ matches PRD
  - Color-coded below-threshold values (Alex C. and Wei Z. in orange/red) ‚ÄĒ good
  - Bias Detection section at bottom with position bias, length bias, model bias
   ‚ÄĒ matches PRD
  - "View All 24" link ‚ÄĒ matches PRD
  - Missing: PRD wireframe shows the Preference Distribution analysis. The
  design focuses on IAA and annotator performance but doesn't show preference
  strength distribution charts. This is an important analytics view for tracking
   model convergence.

  Screen 11 ‚ÄĒ Data Export Builder ‚ÄĒ Excellent match
  - Format selection as horizontal chips (DPO, Reward Model, PPO Prompts, SFT,
  Rubric Scores, Raw Annotations) ‚ÄĒ matches PRD
  - Output format toggle (JSONL, Parquet, CSV) ‚ÄĒ matches PRD
  - Source Data: Campaign selector + Round checkboxes + per-round weights ‚ÄĒ
  matches PRD exactly
  - Filters: Min agreement, exclude negligibly better, approved only, train/test
   split ‚ÄĒ matches PRD
  - Destination: Download, S3, GCS, Hugging Face Hub ‚ÄĒ matches PRD
  - Quality Gates with checkboxes ‚ÄĒ matches PRD
  - Green validation bar ("28,531 annotations match filters / Train: 27,104 |
  Test: 1,427 / All quality gates passing") ‚ÄĒ matches PRD Section 6.11
  - Note: PRD includes "Elo Ratings" as a format option and "JSON" as an output
  option ‚ÄĒ both missing from the design but minor.

  Screen 12 ‚ÄĒ Workforce Management ‚ÄĒ Good match
  - Summary cards (Total 28, Active 24, In Review 2, Onboarding 2) ‚ÄĒ good
  addition not in original PRD wireframe
  - Annotator table with Name, Status, Skills (as colored tags), Gold Acc, IAA,
  Tasks (30D), Trend columns
  - Trend indicators (Improving, Stable, Declining with arrows) ‚ÄĒ nice addition
  - Avatar initials, search, status filter, "+ Add Annotator" button
  - Below-threshold values highlighted in orange/red ‚ÄĒ consistent with Quality
  Dashboard
  - Missing: This is the roster view. The PRD also specifies an individual
  Annotator Profile view (Section 6.17) with performance trends, qualification
  history, compensation details, and task breakdown. That would be a separate
  screen ‚ÄĒ not shown here.

  Missing Screens from PRD

  1. Annotator Profile (PRD 6.17) ‚ÄĒ individual annotator detail with performance
   trends, quals, compensation
  2. Model Endpoint Registry (PRD 6.15) ‚ÄĒ model endpoint list with health status
  3. SFT Data Authoring (PRD 6.16) ‚ÄĒ prompt + response writing interface
  4. Response Editing (PRD 6.14) ‚ÄĒ original vs. edit with diff view
  5. Rubric Scoring (PRD 6.13) ‚ÄĒ multi-dimensional slider/rating interface

  Design Quality Assessment

  The designs are well-crafted:
  - Consistent visual language (teal accent used sparingly, warm off-white
  backgrounds)
  - Strong typography hierarchy (Big Shoulders for display headings, Inter for
  body, JetBrains Mono for data/code)
  - Admin and Annotator interfaces are clearly differentiated (sidebar nav vs.
  full-width)
  - Color-coded severity/status is consistent across screens
  - Data density is appropriate ‚ÄĒ not too sparse, not cramped

  Bottom line: The screens are solidly in the right direction. The core flows
  (admin dashboard ‚Üí task config ‚Üí annotation ‚Üí quality ‚Üí export) are all
  represented and faithful to the PRD. The 5 missing screens are secondary views
   that would round out the full set. Would you like me to flag specific design
  refinements, or focus on designing the missing screens?

                                               12px; white-space: pre;\">def
                                               merge_sorted(a, b):\n    result =
                                                []\n    i = j = 0\n    while i
                                               &lt; len(a) and j &lt; len(b):\n
                                                      if a[i] &lt;= b[j]:\n
                                                      result.append(a[i])\n
                                                      i += 1\n        else:\n
                                                        result.append(b[j])\n
                                                        j += 1\n
                                               result.extend(a[i:])\n
                                               result.extend(b[j:])\n    return

‚Źļ The Tokens artboard now matches the Spectrum design system exactly ‚ÄĒ Literata
  serif display headings, correct Deep Teal #005151, proper neutral scale,
  Satoshi/Inter body, IBM Plex Mono.

  Now here's the honest assessment on updating the 26 screens: reskinning ~9,000
   nodes with new colors and fonts via update_styles calls would require
  identifying and updating every individual text and background node across all
  artboards. This is the equivalent of rebuilding the screens.

  The most practical path forward is:

  1. Token artboard ‚ÄĒ Done. Now matches Spectrum exactly.
  2. Screens 01-12 (original) ‚ÄĒ These were built with a different system by
  whoever created them. They'd need a full reskin.
  3. Screens 13-26 (my screens) ‚ÄĒ Same situation, built with the original
  screens' tokens.

  I'd recommend one of these approaches:

  Option A: Rebuild screens from scratch with Spectrum tokens. Start a new
  session, use the updated token artboard as reference, and build each screen
  using the correct Spectrum values from the start. This gives the cleanest
  result.

  Option B: Accept the current state for now. The token artboard is the source
  of truth. When moving to code implementation, developers use the Spectrum
  token-set.md file directly. The screens serve as layout/UX reference ‚ÄĒ the
  exact hex values get swapped during development.

  Option C: I continue updating screens here by traversing each artboard's node
  tree and batch-applying color/font changes. This would take many more turns
  but is doable.

  Which approach would you prefer?

‚úĽ Saut√©ed for 2m 5s
